Oh, children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, according to its conclusion and through my explanations and declarations, it appears to me that you will be able to grasp what I wish to convey to you in this treatise, which is a part of surgical operation.
Now the surgical operation is almost lost in our region and in our time, so that the science of it has perished, and its knowledge remains hidden; and there remain only a few brief descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been corrupted by many errors and obscurities, so that the intentions of it are closed off and its power and art are stretched out.
And it appears to me that you will revitalize the ancient order of this treatise through the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and for that, you should come with the forms of the instruments of cauterization and other tools of the work, as is necessary for addition to the declaration and preparation of what is to be done.
However, the reason why a good craftsman is not found with his own hand in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long and requires its actor to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which Galen knew well, so that he could know the joints of the members and their forms, and their conjunction and separation; and have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and ligaments, and their number, and the arrangement of them; and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their efflux.
And therefore says Hippocrates that with a small name one can accomplish much, but most of all in the work of the hand.
But we have already said this about him in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about anatomy as we have described it, will certainly fall into error by which men are killed, just as I have seen many of them, because some are formed in this science and then stray from that true science and experience.
For I saw a foolish and experienced doctor who had inserted an abscess into the throat of a woman, and had cut through some arteries in the throat, so that a great deal of blood flowed out and the woman died among others.
And I saw another doctor who told him to pull out a stone from a man's bladder, which he had processed in his state, and the stone was large, and it came to him and he extracted that stone with a piece of the intestines, so that that man died on the third day.
And I have already cried out against it, and saw that because of the largeness of the stone and the condition of the patient, he knew in advance that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and then operated on a blacksmith's leg which was broken in the joint; and the doctor prepared himself with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, over the wound, with pulleys and astels with strong tension, and did not give the wound any breath.
And then he loosened the bandage according to his desires, and then released the ligature, and then left it untied for some days, and commanded that we loosen the tie; and thus it happened that the joint and leg became inflamed, and ultimately led to perdition.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to loosen the tie, and he gained tranquility and eventually became free from his pains.
But however, corruption had already been confirmed in the member, so that it could not be restrained and did not cease to corrupt the member until the patient was endangered.
And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous abscess and it became ulcerated within a few days, until the wickedness of it increased with its lord.
Which is because the cancerous tumor is pure of melancholic humor, so that it does not need to be treated with iron throughout, but rather should be considered as a member which suffers from being totally attacked.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you to divide the surgical operation into two parts: one is in the operation which is associated with health, and the other is in the work where danger lies in the greater dispositions.
And I have already existed in every place of this book where the operation is one in which there is error and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to keep this and avoid that, so that foolishness does not obstruct the way to speak and to deceive.
And therefore take your own arms with solicitude and protection of God, and your own patients with felicity and firmness.
And use the best means by the grace of God to avoid losing health and the noble succession, and abandon the terrible diseases of difficult healing, and hold your own arms from this which makes you fear, so that your situation remains in your faith and in your name does not deceive you: because it is more remaining to your glory, and all the more in this world and forever in your sanctity.
Galen already said in some of his own writings: "Do not heal bad illnesses, because bad doctors are not named."
And I have divided this book into three chapters.
The division of the book begins, and the first part of the first chapter. The first chapter, arranged from head to foot, in the forms of instruments and ironwork of cauterization, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on drying and piercing, and on cupping, wounds, and extraction of splinters and similar things, entirely chaptered and ordered in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on curing of torsion and similar things; chapter ordered from head to foot, and in the forms of instruments.
You should know the quality of the joints of that cauterization and the nonuments of it, and in what composition it is prohibited to cauterize.
Therefore I say that the sermon on the quality of the joint of cauterization and its nonument is a long and prolix discourse, subtle by science, and secret and hidden; and already many wise men have spoken about it, and among them there has been disagreement, and for my part, I will not venture to recount all their sermons, fearing prolongation.
And therefore I say that cauterization agrees with all universal composition universally, which is in matter or its matter, except for two compositions, which are compositions without material.
In the dry and withered composition with material it will desiccate; because some say that cauterization is beneficial to that, and others say the opposite of that, that cauterization is not suitable in a disease which is due to quality and dryness, for nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that the diseased part, which is hot and dry, should be healed with heat and dryness.
And you will find that the one who says the opposite of that is wrong, for through cauterization it is made to heal in all hot and dry diseases that are found in the bodies of men; because when you compare the human body and its humors with the composition of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I say by the sermon of that, that experience has already shown me several times to uncover.
But however it is not necessary that what has already been explained and exercised in the chapter on cauterization should come again over this, for I have already known the diversity of the composition of men and the disposition of diseases in their members, and the causes of those, and the accidents of theirs, and the space of time of those.
But in other compositions, there is no fear for you, and most of all in cold and humid diseases, because already all doctors have agreed on those, and are not discordant in the treatment with cauterization in those.
And know, children, that from the secret of healing by cauterization with fire and the goodness of it, there is something more about cauterization with medicine combined, because the fire is simple, the action of which does not affect except the member that is being cauterized, and does not harm another member adjusted to it but with a small injury.
But the action of combined medicine reaches that member which is distant from it, and very easily brings disease to a difficult-to-heal member and very easily causes harm.
But the fire, due to its sublimity and good substance, does not do this except in a superfluous way. And it is already known to us by experiment and the length of service in studying the art above the truth of causes; and therefore I am excused for the length of the sermon. But if it were not that it is not read in your free book in this pause, I would reveal to you a secret hidden with the fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and its expulsion by which diseases are expelled, with a philosophical and demonstrative sermon, which would be sharpened in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time when it is convenient to perform cauterization and pause for the best time of spring.
And I say that cauterization is convenient at any time, because the harm caused by the accidental timing is submerged in the joint of what is attracted to the cauterization, and most of all if the cauterization is for pains or necessary pains, strong and fierce, which do not suffer tardiness because it is feared that those who bring evil may come, which is greater than a small harm entering through time.
And thus it does not occur in your minds, or, children, that this is not esteemed except by the common people and foolish doctors, for it is that to that disease which is healed by cauterization there is no reduction at all times, and they pause on the consequence.
And the cause is not thus as they say, for cauterization is nothing but a place of medicine that alters the composition and dries up the humors which are the cause why pains come.
But however, cauterization exceeds medicine by the will of its virtue and the grandeur of its lord.
And it is possible that its disease may return at some hour of time, according to the composition of the patient and the location of its disease, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of it from the accumulation of superfluities there, and what has been gained through its acquisition in foods and similar causes; but if the disease in which cauterization is administered is a subtle disease in a member with few superfluities and humors, as with cauterization for toothache and similar pains, it is possible that this pain will not return in full, but rather becomes small.
And it is also common saying that cauterization is the ultimate remedy of medicine, and it is a saying that is most true, not to what they understand in it, because they believe that there is no healing that is beneficial through medicine or any other cause approaching cauterization.
And the cause is contrary to that; and I understand that cauterization is the ultimate remedy of medicine not only when we administer the healing methods in some diseases, and those medicines do not concur, and approaching the end of the cause, one administers cauterization, and it proves to be beneficial. And from now on, know that cauterization is the ultimate remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand as common and foolish among doctors.
And the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and its sublime substance.
And they said that the place of cauterization does not make a difference, as it is not absolutely true, because you have already proven and proved that it does not make a difference in some bodies except for others, and cauterization with gold is good and better than with iron as they said; but however when you do cauterization with fire using gold, it is not declared to you, because it is hidden according to the quantity that you want by the roughness of the gold, and since you prepare to receive heat; and if you adjust above it ignition so that the gold melts in the fire, and the craftsman sees through the occupation of that.
And therefore it is necessary to perform cauterization with iron more lightly and more precisely in order to achieve the rightness of operation.
And I have already organized this chapter on cauterization according to chapters, and I have organized those from head to foot, in order that the demanding one may be satisfied with it.
The First Chapter.
This cauterization is applied to the humidification and coldness on the upper part of the head, which has two causes: one cause being soda and another being a great flow of rheumatic fluid, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears that are fluent, and a great deal of sleepiness, and toothaches, and pain in the jaw, and universally all diseases that come through coldness, such as paralysis, sodomy, apoplexy, and similar things in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is as follows: first, I command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine in the morning, for three or four nights, according to what the disease demands and the age and habit of the patient.
And then I command him to shave his head with a razor, and after that make a section between the hairs on top of his head, and place it on a well-crafted bench, so that he may rest his head on his own feet.
And then pause the razor's edge against the tip of your nose, right between the eyes. But when the fire is reached, mark that place with a tent, and then ignite the cauterization oil of which this is the form:
And then pause that oil on the marked place with a tent, in such a way that it descends, by which your own hand is gradually constrained, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand lightly and look at the place, and if you see that some quantity of bone is already uncovered from the head, such as the amount of grain in errors, then raise your hand and if it is not returned to the iron, use another one that is not chilled, until what I have said to you is seen.
And then take a small amount of salt and dissolve it on the place and let it sit for three days.
And then apply to it a poultice of beggar's ticks and let it sit on the wound until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with four-fold medicine, so that it may be healed.
And they said that as long as the wound remains open, so much the better it is for the cauterization to be applied, because it is more effective and beneficial.
And they said that some of them were cauterized in the cord into the bone, and kept the cauterization until it was absorbed by some part of the specificity of the bone.
And then be rubbed with that which is adapted to the bone, and then be cured.
And others said that with the cauterization, it will reach the end, until it presses strongly on the bone, until the bone cracks, and this is the form of little alfalfa. And they say that from that place, the fumes of the head will evaporate.
And then the open wound should be kept for a long time, and after that it should be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cauterization do not seem right at all, except in certain men according to the way of fear; and leave that, I say, is better for health when it is, because the head is revealed by solution of continuity, as we have testified in other members, and even more so when the patient's head is of a free nature.
And the first species of cauterization is more saved and better, as I say; and from that house and with that work, health ensues.
Second Chapter.
On the Cauterization of the Head.
When in the entire head chronic and long-lasting pain occurs, and this is prolonged in the patient, and uses of warps, cochias, capipurges, emplausters, guats, cadels, and gualinas, and similar things, and most especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery which does not benefit him at all, then consider that whether the head of the patient is of strong creation in his nature; and if it is not free and finds a great deal of coldness, then he cauterizes another cautery, leaving just a little bit. And then cauterize that on the horn of his head with another cautery until the cord is parted. Cut the cord and have it revealed on the bone the quantity which we have recounted, and cauterize that with one cautery in the back part of the head, in the place called "vas", where the wind is paused. And let your hand be in that way, and do not uncover the bone, for the patient by this will feel a great deal of diverse pain different from all other head cauteries.
And you will say that this cautery is in its place, for it is necessary to cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput with a more subtle cautery than that which is used on the middle part of the head; and this is its form.
Third Chapter.
On Cauterization for Headaches not Caused by Ancient Causes.
When headache occurs in the back part of the head, or it is spread into the eye, be evacuated with medicines in the morning, and administer another treatment, which I have said in the divisions of diseases; and if nothing benefits, then cauterization in that place is done in two ways: either by medicine acute and combined, or by iron.
But the cauterization by medicine combined is that you take a sweet of aloes, and soak it in water, and abscind the extremities of it from both ends. And then cut the location of pain in the temple with a blunt lancet until a small pit is made, and it is hidden.
And then apply it to the place with a stopper made of descending constriction, and leave it for three hours; and then remove it and treat the aloes, and leave the wound open for two or three days, and then apply a poultice on top submerged in mud until the place becomes firm.
And then cure that with four-fold medicine, so that it may be healed.
And if you wish, do this with some combined medicines that I have written in the two treatises on combined medicines.
But the cauterization by iron, according to this manner: ignite by the cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called "claw's claw", because the head of it is like a shape of a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small elevation.
And then place the iron on the location of the pain, and hold your hand - so that it is not absorbed by the cord that is left - and turn the small iron gradually with speed.
And if the quantity of it that is absorbed by the specificity of the cord is as great as the majority of it, and lift your hand so that the artery which is left is not absorbed, lest there come a flow of blood.
And then soak the poultice in saltwater and place it on the location, and leave it for three days; and then apply a mullet poultice wrapped in mud, and then cure with four-fold medicine until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize the extremity of the cutlery according to the cautery, and beware of cutting off an artery in this not ancient headache properly.
Fourth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Ancient Headaches.
When you treat headaches with what we have said in the previous treatment and in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not benefit, and sometimes the disease is so severe that it does not reach the point where we have described the first cautery by medicine or by fire, then it is necessary to ignite the cutlery cautery until it is white, because you signify on the location of pain with a line of length which is most of the digit or what it may be; and place your hand for one moment and strengthen that until you cut off the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which is modified by mastication, and that the lacrimal duct not be absorbed and the nerves that accompany that, and that no spasm ensues.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut off, for in the cutting off of it there is fear, and especially to him who ignores this process and does not study or practice; and leave the operation at the beginning.
And you will come to remember the regimen of accidental bleeding from the artery according to your own manner in this very book.
And if you see that this disease does not yield to this cautery and you see the patient's body is tolerable, then cauterize it in the middle part of the head as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we have said in the chapter on stretching of artery with two handles, and this is the better cautery and most concurrent.
Fifth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Earaches.
When in the ear there is pain caused by cold and it is treated with laxative causes and with other treatment which I have said in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one called "puncta", of which this is the form:
And then apply the puncta to the ignition, and be brought around the entire ear as a wheel is revolved, or in the circuit of each example if the pain is in each. And then stretch yourself with the cautery of the root of the ear little by little until you have marked the location with a tent.
And if the cautery of these dots is applied to the entire ear, and in each place, and then cure the locations until they are healed.
Sixth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Torture.
Torture which is cured and by cauterization it is not but of the species which come from flux, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that comes from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of torture with jarrings and capipurgisms and guarguarisms, and your treatment does not confirm, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: the first on the root of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third at the conjunction of two lips.
And then pause your cautery on the contrary side of the ailing part, for softening does not come but on the opposite side that appears to be healing.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cautery on the right side of the extremity of the ear, slightly above the horn of the head, and in the temple another one, the length of which is according to the length of the thumb's joint, and then place your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the cord's specific part is consumed.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species of the cutlery, the form of which is placed before us. But however subtle it may be, that a little bit is as you see it; and it is necessary to cut off the superfluous thickening a little.
And then cure the location with what is before us, until it is healed.
Seventh Chapter.
On Cauterization for Ancient Apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it with what we have said, and your treatment does not confirm, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize that with four cauteries: on all the horns of his head; and with a cautery in the middle part of the head, as we have said; and with another one in the occiput. And the manner of the cautery is made according to what was previously said.
And it is cauterized on the mouth of the stomach; and this is the last one; and then it should be cured with what proceeds.
Eighth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Oblivion caused by Flux.
It is necessary to give the patient in the beginning large jarrings and pills of purging medicines.
And then shave the head of the patient and apply an ointment to the occiput, as described in the treatise on ointments.
And pause it for a few days, because this is the manner of the cautery. And do so according to that order which I have already said.
And thus, if it is well healed by those means; and otherwise, then do so to the three cauteries in the back part of his head, which are descendants from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the neck. And pause between each cautery the thickness of the finger, and then cure the cautery with what has proceeded.
But if you wish to add more and the patient is tolerating it well, then do so to the middle part; and if you wish for even greater addition, then immediately cauterize that on both horns.
And then cure that until it is healed; and be the cautery olive-colored according to the form previously given.
Ninth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Paralysis and Softening of the Entire Body.
Take care to process the head with jarrings and with what we have said; and then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with a cautery in the middle part of the head, and with another one on all the horns of the head, and with another one on the back part of it, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the disease of softening of the body of many and the patients are tolerating well, but the disease is strong, then cauterize that with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and gradually with one cautery until the cord's movement of life is consumed, and lift up your hand. And then cure that until it is healed, and this be olive-colored cauterization.
Tenth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Epilepsy.
No is cauterized the epileptic, but that epilepsy is caused by flux.
And thus, it is necessary to purge the brain of him at the beginning with jarrings and with other treatment which we have said in the division when the patient is great and is tolerant except for the exemption of medicines.
And if the child who cannot tolerate medicines, then administer guarguarisms and mastiguoars as purgatives, before this for several days, with good food.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with one cautery in the middle part of the head according to the previous manner, and another one on the occiput, and each horn of the head is cauterized. And if the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize that with the cauteries which I say, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the back.
And be olive-colored according to what has been previously said.
But if the patient is a child, then pause on a subtle cautery according to this manner.
Eleventh Chapter.
On Cauterization for Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted and flux is gross, then cauterize that with the cauteries which we have said in having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity that declines into melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink water that purifies the brain of it according to what has preceded in the division.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then make a tortoise shell decently made of it over the circle, and then place that in the middle part of the head.
And the patient should be seated comfortably, and held by all parties.
And then apply a poultice; and it is more worthy of an ancient border of sheep's wool. And warm that over the fire with a tempered heat by measure, which said enough when it is more in it. And then put that in the middle part of the head of him in the circle, and let it be there until it is cooled.
And do this with the patient for a whole week once, with another regimen of it good until it is healed; or if you wish, cauterize that by making small points according to what is most of it, so that you hold your hand with a cautery thus ordered: this is a species of cauterization which moistens the brain with equality.
And then put that in a cloth or in gray gauze, wrapped around it.
Twelfth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Water that Descends into the Headache.
When you are declared the beginning of water in the head for the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to drink to the patient water that purifies the head of it, and guard against all humidity.
And make that sweat in a bath for several days.
And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle part of the head; and then cauterize that with two cauteries on both temples if it is the beginning of water in two heads, or of one side if it is the beginning of water in one head.
And then cut all the veins and arteries that are left by the cord; and let the cauteries be in that length in the latitude of the temples.
And guard yourself from fluxes of blood when it is being cauterized; and if you see any bleeding from him, stop it with some medicine which is at your disposal.
And you will find wisdom in the extraction of arteries and in the absorption of those and caution against bleeding.
And some times it is cauterized on the cervical vertebrae left between two bones with two cauteries gradually produced.
Thirteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Old Tears.
When tears of the head are ancient and hardened through the veins and arteries which are in the manifest place on the outside of the head, and it is verified that this is superfluous watery flux, then cauterize that with the cautery which we have recounted in the chapter of the beginning of water descending into the head, and with a cautery in the middle part of the head and two cauteries in the cervical vertebrae left between two temples, and with two cauteries in the cervical vertebrae left between two bones. And if you need addition, then cauterize that on the entire back of the head above the forehead with a small cautery.
Fourteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Stench of Nose.
When you treat that with water which we have said in the division and it does not improve your treatment, then prepare and give to drink to the patient the cohies for three nights; and then shave the head of him, and cauterize it with a white cautery and an olive-colored cautery. And then cauterize that with a clove-shaped cautery and two cauteries on both forehead areas, just above the hairline.
And guard yourself from cutting into the artery, lest you hurt it.
And of the clove-shaped cautery, this is the form.
Fifteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization for Softening of Eyelids of the Head.
When the eyelid of the head is softened by disease or humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery having this lunary shape; and this is the form of it:
And if you wish, cauterize that on both forehead areas a little with two cauteries in all parts, and let them be extended from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the quantity of the forehead.
And do not press too hard with your hand and the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid is habituated.
Sixteenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Eyelid of the Head when the skin is transformed into inner parts and pushes the head.
When the skin of the head is transformed into inner parts just as it pushes the head, then cauterize those in two manners, either by fire or by a medicine that combines.
If by a cautery of fire, command the patient beforehand to wash his skin thus as those who cleanse it, until they are prolonged and equalized; and if you push that which makes them swell, then take away their swelling, you strengthen the head of him with a bandage so that it is not hurt until the skin is born.
Then when they are born and equalized, then pause the patient's head in your sight, and then sign on the eyelid of his head with a tenta, with a signal which is according to the figure of a mertal leaf, and let it be the beginning of the signal just above the skin.
And then put a cloth wrapped in alum or in mucilage of pellitory on the head.
And then ignite the cautery which is this shape of it.
And then cauterize on the figure which you have signaled, little by little, in many times, until the surface of the cord is burned just like a leaf of myrtle, all appearing properly.
And the sign of health from this work is that you see the eyelid of the head already contracted and the skin of it elevated above the point of the head.
And then elevate your hand and let it be for three days, and then pause on the cloth with a border until the scar is eradicated. And then cure that with an ointment until it is healed.
But if some cause returns to the skin and causes swelling again, and the eyelid is softened, then do it again as you did first time.
But if the skin is in the eyelid left behind, then cauterize that until it is elevated to its natural place and equalized, so that the skin does not push against the head.
But the cautery with a medicine that combines is what you command the patient to wash his skin until it is prolonged and equalized, and then make a cloth of paper in the shape of a leaf of myrtle.
And then take one ounce of known salt and one ounce of living cause. The end! And thus it is, and then mix those causes well, and make this with a feast in order that it may not be cooled; and then spread water on the paper which is made in the shape of a leaf of myrtle, and pause that over one head or both heads; and pause behind the head cloth wrapped in alum, and the patient's head be in your sight.
And then pause the said thing on the medicine and press it a little bit, but do not hurt it until the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, because stinging is in it just like from fire.
And thus when the patient perceives that it is getting stinging, then pause the medicine and stop hurting it with your said thing; therefore when the stinging ceases, then wash away the medicine and rinse the head with water; and then consider if the eyelid has already been lifted as washed by fire or incision, because you are satisfied; and if not, then go back to applying the medicine on the location where it has not yet taken effect and do not neglect until your operation is equalized and the head is contracted.
And then pause on the cloth with a border until the scar of adjustment is eradicated, and then cure that with an ointment or another substance until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to keep with diligent vigilance that the medicine does not fall on the head, and if the eyelid some days later becomes softened and some cause of skin pushes into the head, then iterate your medicine on that location where the eyelid has become softened, and just as you did at the beginning, and then apply it again until it is healed.
And this is the shape of a leaf of myrtle.
And know that the heads of men are diversified according to magnitude and smallness, and therefore according to this is made your contraction.
And may not be hidden the way of rectitude from him who studies in this art.
Seventeenth Chapter.
On Cauterization of Fistula that is in the Lachrymal of the Head.
When you cure a fistula with the water that we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not confirm your cure, then be it so that you cauterize that according to this manner: command the patient to pause his head in your sight, and hold his head by some minister between your hands in such a way that it is not hurt nor agitated with his own head.
And then put a cloth wrapped in alum or in mucilage of pellitory on the head of him.
And then ignite the cautery which is this shape:

On the Cure of Alconati.
This disease which is called alconati is nothing but a pus that is situated in the eye, resembling descending water and not being that.
But the manner of acting on it is that you make the patient sit on a well-appointed and straight chair, and then take your own head in two parts and place that in such a way that you see the pus reaching the parts above, and then be dried and not descend, and stop the light, and the patient sees the causes as he would.
And if it does not descend below, know that it is water.
But if the preparation for the descent of the pus is not done with the water as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands and take a subtle spatula and find it on the panniculus cerning a little bit from the continuation of the conjunctiva with the tunic cornea in the crown (into the place that you will see), until the pus is forgotten.
Therefore, when it is forgotten, then you must distill into the eye warm water in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have boiled fenugreek and honey.
And then be cured by other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXIII.
On the Cure of the Water Descending from the Eye.
We have already said the kinds of water in the division and which is suitable for piercing as we declare in sermon, then that according to health.
Then it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands on a chair and bind their own eye tightly.
And then pause on the side of the patient's eye with your left hand if their eye is the left one; or with your right hand if it is the right one.
And then with your right hand take alumina if the eye is left; or with your left hand if it is right.
And then pause the extremity of alumina close to the crown by the thickness of the ray in the album of the eye from the smaller lacrimal part, and then impale alumina with virtue and revolve your hand with it.
And then penetrate into the album of the eye and feel that alumina has already reached the seen cause.
And it is necessary that the measure of the path of alumina to the front be equal to the measure of space which is the diameter of the pupil from the beginning of darkness to the end of blackness, and it is the crown of the eye; for you will see with that pupil by the vision of the eye through the clarity of the tunic cornea.
And then pause alumina in the location where the water is, and then you attract it down once or twice, and thus if the water descends soon, then behold the patient with that on which their vision will soon be, and alumina in its own eye.
And then pause for a moment; thus if the water has descended, then you should place that other time ahead of alumina before it is dropped.
And then when it is dried and does not descend, you should extract alumina with ease, and revolve with it your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a small amount of clear gemstone salt and mix it with that to wash the eye outward; and then pause outside the eye with a cotton or stopper or wool infused in rose oil and albumen of egg white, and bind the eye tightly.
But we and those of our time pause over that which is torn apart with albumen of egg white.
And if it does not obey your alumina at the instrument of the eye by its hardness - for it is one of those men whose eye is very hard - then you must take the spatula which is called "alberid" and this is its form:
And then perforate with that the conjuncture, and do not stop your hand in the hole, and do not be if it is not that you make a way to alumina's subtle place.
And then introduce alumina according to what we have said.
And you must complete the complement of your work, be prepared for the patient's sleep descent made in which they will sleep on their back in a dark room, and be forbidden from all movements.
And pause in the nature of it so that its nature is linked, and do not move their head to the right or left side at all.
And be the bandage according to its disposition within three days.
And then remove that in the dark and expose the fresh vision, and make it see some causes, and then return the bandage within seven days.
And it is not necessary to do that at the time of the cure or soon after infusion. They had need that you avoid this because the water flows more lightly by great and vehement regard.
But if an apostema occurs cautiously, then you must remove the eye before the 7th day, and correct it with water that flows out of the apostema.
Then you will absolve the vision of it and pause on the face of it orally for which the moment is regulated by it for some days, existing in the darkest darkness.
And then be taken away from that great darkness and converted into its own causes.
And know that in alchemy there is no excuse for the disciple's vision a few times, and then you will be brave on the operation.
And it has already been reported to us by some of those who are in the Artach, and one said that fire is made in the Ayrac Magdalen, perforated at which the water is sucked.
But meanwhile you have not seen anything like this in our land which has perfected water, nor do you read about it in some of the ancient books; and it is possible that this is new.
And these are the forms of the species of Magdalen by which one may be above those who ignore them:
And they are made of iron or of earth properly, and they are the extremities of their own with this subtlety triangular, the sharp end just like that is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
On the Cure of Flesh Rot in the Nose.
When in the nose are born various flesh rottings, some of which are caused by some cause resembling that of scorpio's weight or polyp's disease; and this illness is called polyps because it resembles that represented by pey. And in it are cancerous flesh, pale and of a dark color; and in it is that which is not flesh like a lion's color.
Then in that which is not flesh like a lion's color, and is not cancerous or fraudulent, you must make the patient sit between your hands and place them in the sun, and anoint the nose with it, and prick once in those flesh. And then extract that from the outer parts, and then incise with that which you have comprehended from those with a sharp and subtle spatula, one part to the other, until you know that all the flesh is gone; for if there remains any cause by which it can be abscised, then you must ratify that with one of the subtle instruments with ease, until no cause remains. But if the wound begins to bleed or an apostema occurs cautiously, then you must pause at that which is necessary; or it is one of the malignant apostemas, then you must cut and cauterize that until the bleeding stops and all the cavities are gone.
And then be taken away from the nose with an incision, so that the water or wine may flow in. But if the nose is swollen and there is moisture proceeding into the palate, then you will know that it has already been healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you will know that behind it is flesh rot in the bones of the nose to which abscission has not been obtained.
Then it is necessary that you introduce the thread of lead to which there is some thickness, and thrust it into the bone with great force, and pause between each thrust the quantity of said or less, and engender the illness and introduce one extremity of the thread into the nose by means of a ray or another cause which is possible for it.
And when this has been done, then attract the thread of lead into the nose so that it reaches the canals of the nostrils, and let it be situated on the upper part of the nose, because many times the children at school make a similar action, and it is a light cause for one who wants to do so.
And then pause the two extremities of the thread, one extremity that goes out on the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a serration of flesh with the needles that are in the thread, and do this until you know that the flesh is already sewn with the needles of the thread.
And then extract the thread, and pause in the nose near the abstraction of blood for a day or two, and do this for three days or more until the scabbed flesh is all gone from the bones.
And then pause in the nose with a lead tube for several days until it is healed.
But if you find that the cure does not exist, use this one.
And this is the form of the instrument, the cupping vessel maker, with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:
And make it of silver or earth, which resembles a small open lamp, like a small conch shell, and the mouth similarly.
And if you want, make a closed tube like a cane, and the tube of the cupping vessel maker be flat, open; to which there is a handle at the end, with which you will hold that when it is soaked in oil or water that you want from the juices and causes suitable.
Chapter XXV.
On the Worms that are in the Extremities of the Nose.
Many times it is found that a worm is in the extremities of the nose, and it is magnified and multiplied in several days until one can see its regard.
And therefore you must incise that in the beginning of the appearance of it, and eradicate all of that. And then pause over the place or cauterize or medicine which is in place of it.
But if it is delayed in its incision until it is magnified, then consider whether it is lapidated, hard, of dark color and of little sensation; then do not touch that with iron because it is a cancerous apostema; for many times the one who incises this apostema becomes greatly maligned by it against that which had it.
And if the apostema is of lion's touch and not of dark color, and sometimes incision is possible in all that, then evacuate the patient and incise that without fear, and cure the place with what exists and constrains until it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
On the Suture of the Nose and Lips and Ear when Continuity is Dissolved by Wound or Similarity.
Know that when solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, few confer on that operation except in some men.
Then, when you have to deal with some cause of those, consider whether it is a fresh wound with its own blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the wound with suture, and carefully cure that until it is healed.
And if the lips of the solution of continuity are already separated, and each is made whole, then it is necessary that you excise each part of its own cord apparent until no blood flows. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen those, and on top of them sprinkle blood of dragon and well-stretched powder, and pause over the powder a piece of emplastrum diafinicon, or some other of the consolidating plasters, and let that be bound for two days or three, and then remove that and replace it with another plaster and let that remain until the flesh is abscinded, and then cure with scabbing until it is healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the solution of continuity with thread or needles as we have recounted in the suture of the belly, or add the solution of continuity with lead or other materials and make it known.
Chapter XXVII.
On the Extraction of those Causes that come in the Two Lips in the parts behind.
Many times it is found that some men in the parts behind their lips have certain apostemas hard and similar to grass errors, and some are smaller and others are greater.
Then, it is necessary that you convert the lips and fissures each of those hardnesses in all parts, and then fill the place with sagitta powder, well-stretched, until the blood is restrained, and then wash with wine and be careful to cure the place with what exists, until it is healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
On the Incision of the Flesh Adjusted in the Gums.
Great many times nay over the gummed flesh which the ancients called albulus, then it is necessary that you suspend that with a needle or that you hold that with the forceps and incise that as it should be, and let the blood flow or run.
And then pause over the place with sagitta powder or other stiptic or excitatory powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise it secondarily, and cauterize it, for then the cauterization will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
On the Reason of Teeth with Iron.
When on the surface of the teeth in the parts behind and in front, and between the gums are adjusted scorching aspersions, rough, black, and some times are made citrines or green, until it is seen that through this corruption the gums are decayed and the teeth are rough.
And then it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands and pause the head in your own seat, and remove the teeth in which those scorching aspersions and causes appear like sand, until there remains no cause of their own, and this will be done with the blackness and citrinity and other things until they are purified.
Then if this is at the beginning of the reasoning, good it is; and otherwise, then you iterate the reason over those for another day and for the second and for the third until it comes to the final statement in what you want.
And know that teeth have needed many residues of diverse forms and figures according to how it is prepared for your operation. And therefore, because the razors with which the tooth is rasped from the part behind are another kind of razors with which it is rasped between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors should be prepared by you which you will see soon:
Chapter XXX.
On the Eradication of Teeth.
It is necessary that you cure the tooth of its pain with all ease and gentleness in total eradication of it, for there is no cause that can sustain the existence of it when it is eradicated, for it is a sublime substance into which it is excused in the eradication of it.
But it is necessary that when the patient is prepared to eradicate that tooth, you must be firmly certified which is the aching tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and says it is in a healthy tooth, and then you eradicate that one and carefully note that the pain does not cease until the sick and aching tooth is eradicated, for we have already seen this by the operation of barbers.
Then, since you are certified which is the aching tooth, and what you know well, it is necessary that you scrape in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth to the gum of all part, and then carefully remove that with your own hands or with fine forceps little by little until it becomes loose.
And then, with great force hold tight the large instruments for good conversation or strong extraction, and pause the head of the patient between your own hands that you may not hurt them, and carefully remove the tooth in a straight manner so as not to break it, nor give greater pain to the patient.
And then, if not forgotten, take one of those instruments and place it at a distance from the tooth on all sides with ease and effort, removing it as was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is rough or corroded, then it is necessary that you wrap a cloth around it and bind it with a thin thread at its extremity, so that it will not be torn in the hour of your constriction upon it when you take hold.
And it is necessary that you work with great care using a scraper in the circuit of all parts of the gum and preserve your strength so as not to break it and leave a part of it, and return upon the patient for the malice that will be greater than the first pain.
And beware that you do not act like some ignorant barbers in their foolishness and audacity about the eradication of their own patients, for they do not administer what we have recounted; for many times they bring upon men great illnesses which are harder to be torn away, and all or some of those causes, or that extracts it with some bones of the jawbone just as many times we have witnessed.
And then, after the eradication, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar mixed with salt.
And if there is bleeding from it, just like many times there is, then carefully take some quantity of zeig and sprinkle it over the wound, and if that zeig does not help, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and fine tweezers with which the tooth is extracted at the beginning should be long in length, short in handle, and thick, so that they are not doubled when you must work with them.
And should be like times of thick handle so that when you stretch with those they are not doubled, and short in length.
And should be made of Indian steel with handles made of straight extensions, and in the extensions of those some teeth are set which fit into each other and stretch by strong construction, and sometimes the extensions of those have the shape of a bird's beak, specifically that of a ciconia, so it is guarded, and they are of very strong construction.
Chapter XXXI.

When you need to extract the tooth that is broken by some cause, it is necessary that you pause over the place cut with a border for one day or two until the place is mollified; and then carefully grasp with gentle hands or forceps the extensions of which are assembled like the beak of a bird called ciconia or guanta, the form of the forceps:
Their extensions are made behind, just like a lime or an almond.

And it should be of short extension, thick and small, and not curved so that it will not break.

The form of the second instrument is that it should be triangular and have a more subtle extension.

of the triangular extension twisted or short, which has some thickness, and not curved so that it will not break.
