And accordingly push the child into the parts below until it is paused according to what is necessary, and command the woman to compress herself for some time, and if God wills it, the child will soon be forgotten with a lighter emergence.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that sometimes twins are born, and some times three or four, but this is rare and not to be expected; however, there are causes natural, and not living.
And among those, whether they are multiple or single, one umbilical cord, and they are separated by ciphac, distinguish them from the ligament in the navel of each of those And some times they are forgotten thus as one fetus for natural emergence lighter, and some times they are born with non-natural emergence thus as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult to deliver and proceed to what we have said about non-natural figures, then you should cure those as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with ease and subtlety, and in delay, and is skilled according to all figures as it is prepared by nature leading to salvation.
Recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos and Aborted.
Some weeks are formed in one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten days; and it is necessary for me to verify that a woman aborts at the seventh day, and another at the tenth day, which was caused by measurement of the glorious sages.
And all this must be in the science of the midwife because it is a little similar to what has been said, and therefore pause there as much as is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the Extraction of the Fetus when it is Dead.
When you treat the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not yet emerged, and you are forced to use operation by hand, then it is necessary that you consider whether the woman has a healthy virtue and is not afflicted with any of the accidents by which peril is feared for her.
Then it is necessary that the woman be laid down on her back over the bed, and her head inclined downwards, and her thighs elevated.
And the minister should hold her in two parts or be tied down on the bed for that reason, so that the body of her does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And accordingly moisten the mouth of the mare with warm oil, and mullein, and fenugreek, and sesame seed.
And accordingly the midwife should bring her hand with those oils and mullein, and accordingly enter her hand with ease into the mare, and accordingly seek out the exact location where the fingers will be placed on the fetus.
And finding the convenient location: then you should consider if the fetus is prepared to emerge on its head, and accordingly place your fingers in the following locations: on the ears of him, or on the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or below the beard, or in the furcula of him, or in the places proper to the ribs, or below the hypochondria.
But if the emergence is on the feet of him, then in the pentalion or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary to have the fingers of the right hand and pause the curvature of him at that location which is between the digits of the left hand, and enter the hand with ease and place the fingers in one of those locations which we have said, until you reach the cause of the boyd.
And accordingly pause and place another finger, or the third if necessary, in the opposition of him, to attract equalization, and not be extended according to his straightness only.
And it will be good for the whole part, for that reason the emergence of him will be alleviated thus as is done in tooth extraction for the eradication of him.
And it is necessary in him that which is between them that the extension be softened; and if some part of him is retained, then the midwife should bring some of his fingers with oil and enter those expertly and turn with water what is retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is forgotten, then the fingers should be pushed forward until the location where it is more above; and make so that all the fetus is forgotten.
But if the hand is emerged before the other, and it is not possible to reduce that by the contraction of him, then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped around it; and accordingly extract that until all is forgotten, and insert it either in the joint of the hand or in the wrist.
And so it is necessary to do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or if there is contraction in the emergence, or if water is adjusted in the head of him, then it is necessary that you insert between the digits a spatula with spines and cut off the head and extract the water, or use an instrument which is called "alundat", whose form will come from the forms of other instruments in the chapter which is appropriate to this.
And similarly do if the fetus has a large head by nature: and it is necessary that you insert it with an algemate, or take it with an alundat as we have said; and accordingly extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is emerged and contracted at the furcula, then it should be cut open until the humidity which is in the pit is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obedient to emergence, then you should insert the head as soon as possible according to what seems best to you.
And if the afterbirth of the belly is apoplectic or is in him with dropsy, then it is necessary that you perforate that until the humidity which is in him flows out.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the attraction of him is slight and the direction of him to the mouth of the mare is slight.
But if it is contracted in the belly and pit, then it is necessary that you extract that with cloth which you will wrap around your hand, and cut open the belly and pit until the water that is in them runs out.
But if the other members are stiff and turn back to the head, then put your right hand into it; but if the mouth of the mare is swollen, then insert your left hand into the harp and seek out that head, and attract it with the fingers until it enters the mouth of the mare, and accordingly enter one finger or two fingers into him and draw him with those.
And if the mouth of the mare is contracted by apoplectic catarrh which happens to him, then it is necessary that you do not trouble him with this; but rather administer effusion of humid and fatty causes. And administer poultices; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, it should be punctured: and administer water as we have said in the living fetus.
And if this is not possible, then it should be inserted into pessaries, and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave any cause behind the umbilical cord.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer water as we have said for the cure of apoplectic catarrh which happens to the mare.
And if bleeding occurs, then administer in aqueous stiptics and give the other cure.
And you have already seen a woman in whose womb was a dead fetus, and accordingly on that spot another embryo conceived, and accordingly the dead fetus is another. It happened to him, accordingly, after a long time an apoplectic catarrh in his navel; and it swelled until a foul odor began to emit.
And you were called upon to cure him, and treated him for a long time, and the wound was not consolidated.
Then you applied some emplasters of strong attraction to him, and extracted from him one bone, and accordingly passed several days, and extracted another bone; and I was too astonished, as in the womb there is no bone.
And then you thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
So you cleansed the wound, and extracted many bones from him, the woman existing in her own miserable condition, and already living in such a way for a long time, cried out with a little breast.
And I did not consider it strange, but rather because in that is science and aid to what the physician has in his hand to administer cure.
Of the forms of instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of vertebrae with which the mare is opened:
This is the form of strengthener in which are equated the free ones, to which equating are two vertebrae at the two extremities of two feet. However, this vertebra must be more subtle than the strictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood.
And the latitude of each foot is about two digits and the margin of each about one digit, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle part of the two feet are two adjustments of those fixed feet, which are already secured, of which the length is the majority of one palm and a little more, and the latitude of each is about two digits, or a little more.
And these two adjustments are inserted in the mouth of the mare so that it is opened with them when you revolve the two prescribed vertebrae.
Another form similar to that, more subtle and lighter:
Be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of forceps. However, at the end of it there are two adjustments like those times, and the length of these adjustments is about one palm, and the latitude of each is two digits.
And when you want to open the mare with those, then you should cause the woman to sit on a bed with her feet hanging down, opening what is between her thighs. And accordingly, over your hand with the instrument as you make it for forceps equalizing according to the quantity you want of the appreciation of the mouth of the mare until she makes what you want.
The form of vertebrae which was said by the ancients:
Form of impulse by which the fetus is impelled:
Form of accommodation by which the great head is contained:
And it is assembled to forceps which has teeth at the end, just like times, and some times it is made long just like forceps according to this form, just like times, with teeth just like teeth of a reed into which it is inserted and contained. Form of accommodation few:
Form of finger having one spine:
Form of finger having two spines:
Form of spatula having two extremities at which the head is cut off:
Form of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when more species of that are multiplied and prepared by the artisans, as it is easier to their operation and more necessary for men in proportion.
And do not neglect those instruments however small they may seem to you, because the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Of extraction of the umbilical cord.
When the umbilical cord is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary that you order the patient to retain her breath, and accordingly make her cough with conditions, and strengthen your hand over her mouth and nostrils, and if by this means it is extracted, well it is.
And if not, then take a cloth and pierce it in the covering of a hole, and pause in that herb which is used to open the mouth of the mare, such as calamus and rue and anise and chamomile and Arab spices and cassia lignea and St. Andrew's. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the cloth, and pause it over the fire.
And accordingly place a reed cane in the mouth of the mare, and keep it until the vapor comes to the concavity of the mare.
And accordingly make her cough just as we have said, and the umbilical cord is expelled quickly.
But if this cure does not work and the umbilical cord is still retained, then you should order the midwife to submerge her left hand in samian oil or in a mixture of altaic herbs, and accordingly insert it into the confluence and seek out the umbilical cord, and when you have found it, take it and stretch it out gradually. But if it is annexed in the womb of the mare, then insert your hand according to what we have recommended, and when you have found the umbilical cord, extract it little by little according to rectitude, so that the mare does not faint from the vehement attraction. But first, it is necessary to be made pliable on both right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mare is contracted, we have already recommended the cure by coughing and administering medicine with the cloth and herbs.
But if it is not expelled with all the causes which we have recommended, then beware that you do not force anything over there in iteration of abstraction, but rather, it is necessary that what has emerged from him to the mouth of the mare lies at the edge of the woman's bed, and accordingly, plasterize it with a poultice and tetra-pharmacopeia; because that will make it rot away within a few days and be dissolved and expelled.
But when it rots, it is elevated to a bad authority on the head and stomach, and accordingly leads the patient astray; and then it is necessary that sub-fumigations and conveniences be administered to him.
But some of the Ancients have already experimented with sub-fumigation using nitre and dried figs.
Form of instrument by which the woman is sub-fumigated for retention of menstruation and umbilical cord:
Be made of bay or earthenware.
And be placed the slender extremity in the cleft and the broad extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigation be placed on the arms of the fire.
And keep that until the sub-fumigation is consumed and then iterate another.
Of cure for the child's unperforated anus.
Many children are born without anuses, those which have a subtle and opaque covering. Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that subtle covering with her finger; and if not, then pierce it with a sharp spatula, and be careful not to touch the lacet.
And accordingly, pause over that with wool infused in vinegar and oil; and accordingly, cure it with a poultice until it is settled.
But if you fear that it may be obstructed, then pause in the hole a reed cane for many days, and stop when the child will desire to relieve itself.
And if there is obstruction of the anus due to consolidation of wound or apoplectic catarrh; then it is necessary that this consolidation be incised, and accordingly be cured with the water we have said for the cure and with lead.
Of cure for the fistulae which are left behind.
The fistulae which are left behind in the departure, and which are lower than the navel and thicker on the one side or in the space of the one part, near the anus.
And it is a single fistula or several.
And when that nodule is old and flows with white or yellowish liquid, or subtle putridation, and sometimes some of these fistulae are penetrating.
And those that are penetrating are known by what comes out of them through egression and ventosity; and sometimes the patient uses the evacuation of egression, and very little comes out of those worms.
And some of those fistulae occasionally penetrate into the bladder and into the urethra of the penis; and some of those penetrating into the junction of the pelvis and into the notch of the coccyx.
And the way to know if a penetrating fistula is not penetrating is that you put your finger into the anus and then insert a subtle probe of earthenware or iron into the fistula when there is no resistance.
But if there is resistance in that, then insert into it a subtle probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel it at all or there is no discharge of any kind, whether worms or wind, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrating, and accordingly apply the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or urethra of the penis, then the significance of it is that urine will come out of that and prohibition of it at this point so that the place with medicine may be consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the pelvis or bone and causing pain in the circulation, then the sign of it is that the probe will go in here if there is no resistance to the bone, and causing pain in the circulation of the departure; and that from it always putridation appears; and that no remedy is valid in that, nor is it consolidated with a poultice.
And in all those penetrating fistulae there is no complete cure, and the cure of those is tedious and futile labor on the part of foolish doctors who are fixed.
But in that which is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is expected according to what you have recommended, and what you have already proved.
And it is that the patient lies between two cushions over his back and elevates his legs up to them, so that the pelvis are inclined towards the belly of him, and accordingly insert a probe of lead or earthenware into the fistula if there is resistance, until you know the place where the probe will go in.
And if that makes the patient feel a sensation around the anus, then it is necessary that you put your finger into the anus.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe has already gone in and is penetrating, or if you feel between your finger and that siphac or flesh, then you will certainly know that it is penetrating; and accordingly do not trouble yourself with it, as we have said.
But yet some say that it cures in some people at times.
And of the medicine by which one hopes for improvement in that is that you apply a subtle cauterizing fire according to the size of the fistula, as has been previously said, and insert that ignited into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and accordingly repeat that two or three times until you know that all those adjusted fleshy tissues that are similar to the quill of an eagle have become united.
And accordingly cure that with wrapped calkins in parchment until all those adjusted fleshy tissues are united, and accordingly cure that with medicines generating and consolidating flesh, and if it is healed, well it is; and otherwise, then it is not healed at any time by other cures.
And if the probe goes in and does not penetrate into the anus which is in the rectum, and between that and the probe which is a velament of flesh or nodule, and sometimes the fistula opens up on the surface of the codena, then dry out the codena from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it drying with the probe, and be in the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the extremity of the probe goes in, and by the probe is liberated and freed.
And accordingly, purify those fleshy tissues which are assembled like the quill of an eagle and do not remain for any reason.
But if the flow of blood comes and goes between you and your operation when you are purifying those fleshy tissues, then use the remedy that is easiest to apply with the least effort, which is cauterization with fire or sharp medicine, for cauterization with fire adjusts two good habits: so it adjusts the adjusted fleshy tissues, and abscizes the blood by excessive humidity.
And accordingly cure that with wrapped calkins in parchment or in threefold cloth until the wound gets braised, and accordingly cure the wound with poultices of hard flesh that generate and consolidate.
And such medicines in which there is astringency and excess; when that is restored it is healed and you do not fear relapse.
But if the fistula has already gone into the anus and is elongated from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and inquire about it.
And therefore if you feel the probe and it is between you and her a velament of nodule or flesh, and is inclined towards penetration, then there is no operation in that but according to the way of faith and hope.
Which cause is to be administered in that place by one of three ways: either to cauterize it as we have said; or to dry out that part until you achieve the conquest of it so that it becomes possible for you to insert some and the natural cure is achieved; and do not proceed with any drying out because you will not inscribe the lacert containing the anus, and it will occur over the patient's consent; and accordingly cure that with water as we have said, which will be quite healthy; or elongate that velament and dry out that part up to the prop of the anus, as we have said, or with a probe or another instrument of sharp extremity, and accordingly purify those fleshy tissues that are in the section until you can make an incision; and accordingly strive to restore all the wound with drying out, and if the opening above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open on the side of the anus, and it will be easier for the patient. And in some cases the fistula is closed by this method: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is in the latz of the anus around the surface of the body with the codena and on the margin of the anus, then take hold of a perforated extremity, which is like an awl that prepares the skin according to this form:
and insert it into that faithful wrapping of vein or around those; and accordingly insert the probe with faith in the fistula until you achieve the conquest of it.
But if it is penetrating into the margin of the anus proper to the inside, then you take out the vein from that hole as if you insert your finger into the anus; and pull out the extremity of the vein and adjust the two extremities together, and strengthen each one, and leave water for a day or two, and when more you insert the vein into the flesh, strengthen it until those fleshy tissues are inserted between the two extremities of the vein which fall.
And accordingly cure the wound so that it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in any way you have prepared for it, but not so much that it reaches the anus, because it is not your business to do that; and accordingly make it healed with water as we have said.
The shape of the spatula with which the fistula is punctured: its curvature is very sharp on one side and not sharp at all on the other side, so that you do not insert what is not necessary, just like sometimes.
Of stitching of hemroids in which blood flows during the incision of those.
Hemroids are according to two ways, for either they are between the anus resembling like those of charcoal, or those which are like a grass of rashes. And those are small and large, and the blood flows from them always and is one, and many, and outside the anus, and in its extremities.
But those that are outside the anus are according to the months of little moisture, from which flows a yellowish water or a small amount of blood with continuous pus, and according to the color of the body.
And the cure for that which is outside the anus is to command the patient to settle down and to be expelled into the anus until the anus opens and the hemroids appear before you. Then you will cut and suspend with scissors or whatever you have those on your fingernail, and accordingly cut off the roots of those.
But if the scissors are not taken to those because of the humidity and softening of them, then take those with a rough cloth or with a piece of cotton or with a woolen rag, and pull out those with the aforementioned fingers, and accordingly cut off those and powder some powders on top of them nearby the incision, so that they are adapted to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those as it is preceded in the chapter of cauterizing. And accordingly cure those with another cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey evacuation, then cleanse the patient with a small amount of cistern in the cistern where there is slight biting, and wash him with that water that is in the anus and that will obey evacuation slightly when the patient is evacuated.
But if the hemroids are outside the anus, then the cause of them is slight, and it is that you take those with your fingernail or with scissors, and cut off those, and accordingly cure those with water as we have said until they are healed.
And whoever will have incision, should administer suture of theirs according to this method: take a faithful wrapping and insert that into the needle and accordingly pull out the hemroids at the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the needle in the root of the other part, and wrap the two extremities of the thread in the part most left behind of the needle, and so latitudinally; and strengthen the hemroid with a strong stitch, and accordingly remove the thread and extract the needle.
And do this with all of them, and leave one of those alone and do not cook it, so that the superfluity of blood flows from that.
And accordingly place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the anus, and place that on the anus and command the patient to rest. And accordingly leave that until it is hardened, and when it has hardened, cure those with poultices or with another cure until they are healed.
And since they are so old and not valid in that medicine, then you must scrape those with the point of a spatula or with your fingernail until they become moist and the scab above is prevented from forming; and accordingly cure those until they are consolidated.
Then you must scrape those with reason more violent than the first time until there is no blood and they are exfoliated; and accordingly cure those until they are healed.
Know that Almesmir is the key, and it is not so unless there are notes redone according to the color of the body resembling a head of clavicle, and it is made throughout the body and most in the parts left behind the weights and the dits, and thereby one must follow the pain through the love.
And then it is necessary to cut off that which is in the circle of the key, and be held with forceps or scissors, and be eradicated from its root; and accordingly cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize it according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing.
But of verruca is a small rough wart-like prominence that is fistulated and rounded on the surface of the body, and many times it appears in children's hands.
And the cure for that is to spread and cut off that, or to strengthen it with a thread or with a cloth until it hardens. And if you wish, cauterize it, as we have said, with fire or sharp medicine.
But a formic is a small prominence that is fatty or fistulated large on the surface of the body moving towards the anus, and when the heat finds it, it appears like a biting of an ant, and is made around the body.
And the cure for it is that you take a quill of goose or of wolverine, and it be strong, and place it on the formic until it contains the circle of the quill around the parts of it; and accordingly revolve your hand with the quill until you cut off what is in the circuit of the formic, and place it in the anus of the flesh, and thereby eradicate the formic from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a clay or iron quill according to this form:
Be the upper part of the quill thin and subtle, not perforated, wrapped in such a way that on the said part of it is ablated and the rotation of it.
And if you wish, cauterize the ant according to what is said before in the chapter on cauterizing.
The Form of the Instruments that are administered to give Cistern.
Sometimes cistern is made of silver or lead or clay melted or hammered; and sometimes it is made with small and large instruments according to those which are administered, for that which is administered in the cure of small children is small; and of those whose anus is rough or painful, their cisterns are small.
The Form of Cistern Great and Little.
The head of the quill above, in which the bag is tied, should be wide according to this method; and there should be a distinction at the place where the bag is tied just like sometimes.
And the extremity of it most below, which is inserted into the anus, should be blunt (so it is not open) very much like a lion, going back to subtlety; and on one side of it there are two holes, and on the other side one hole, and the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and slightly larger than small.
And the bag should be in which medicines from the bladder of an animal or from sheep's wool are placed, and the root of it should be a palm.
And it should be pierced with many holes just like it is rolled up; and if the space which is between the holes is as thick as said.
And accordingly insert into those holes a strong thread of raw thread which is of ten threads, or around those; and adjust the bag with that; and when it is placed in there the bag should be tight at the head of the cistern between two distinct parts with strong constriction, and accordingly cauterize each hole: But the quality of cauterizing is that you fill the bag with medicine, which should be warmed according to the quantity of the patient's tolerance; and beware that it is not too hot nor too cold.
And accordingly the patient should be raised over his back, and lift his legs up high and place something flat underneath it on which men or a lansol rest; and accordingly anoint the extremity of the cauter with oil or album of wheat or mucilage of fenugreek or similar substances; and accordingly insert that into the anus with ease, and accordingly the minister should take the bag and expel that with two hands and sometimes with vehemence until it is evacuated in the bedpan all that is in the cistern; and accordingly remove the cistern and the patient will lift his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces him to sleep, let him sleep as long as he can; and if he sleeps with that all night, it is even later in judgment.
But if you cauterize that in diseases of stool evacuation and the patient's sleep is disturbed, then you must repeat the cauterization until he is cured.
And if in the anus there are hemroids or apoplastic lesions, then you should use a cistern that is very subtle and lion-like, from among those with which children are cisternized.
The Cure of Plagues.
And so I have said in the division of the cure of plagues what is necessary for the free man, and I say thus the cure of those with me and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that plagues are diversified according to what the plagues are made and according to the place on which the plagues are placed.
And the causes by which many times plagues are made are just like a blow of pepper, or incision of space or of cote, or percussion with lance, or with fist, or with arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the parts of the body are like a plague which lies on the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the thigh, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I recommend the cure for some plagues by which you pause that reasoning and rule over other plagues.
And I begin with the plagues of the head, simple ones, for the memory of the compound ones will come at the beginning of the fourth chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to a blow of pepper or similar, and if the wound has already opened up just a little bit and it is a big plague and you fear that there may be an apostema forming, then you should take care of it and perform cephalic bleeding as soon as possible, and do not delay; and extract blood from it according to the quantity of its virtue, unless there are other causes prohibiting bleeding, especially if the blood that has flowed out of the plague is little.
And perform the bleeding on the opposite side of the affected part; and beware that the patient does not get filled up with blood, nor eat nor drink strong foods.
But if there is any prohibition from the minority, then it should be reduced in food and not approach meat nor wine.
And place on the plague, if an apostema is forming cautiously, apply oil of roses or wine in which it is stipticated.
But if it is certain that an apostema is forming cautiously, then place on the plague, if it is fresh with its own blood and the air has not changed that powder which I recommended earlier in small amounts.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on it some poultice until it is healed.
But if the plague is great or is due to incision of space and similar things, and the lips of it are not adjusted for pus, then adjust those with a suture according to how I recommend for the suturing of theirs.
But if the plague has already been discovered from the bone and pen, and there is no retention of it but only a small suspensor, then cut off that and accordingly cure the plague with medicines and restore the flesh in its proper place, and command the patient to eat foods in which there is grossness: caps and forms like theirs, until they are composed.
And if you find in the wound putrefaction and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut off all that putrid part and remove it, and accordingly cure what remains.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood can flow and it is not abscessed by medicines, then you should inquire about the artery, and if you find that one which is not abscessed, then cut off that with a spatula or tie it; and if necessity demands that what we have said does not come to pass, then you should cauterize in order for the blood to be abscessed.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is slight; therefore you can powderize on those this powder, for it will consolidate that before the air changes those.
And the method of the powder is this: take oil from a dragon's wound, one part, blood of a dragon, two parts, and non-extinguished charcoal, three parts; mix it all well and grind it finely, and fill the wound with it, and compress it with good constriction until it adheres well to that place, and coagulates with the blood.
And accordingly strengthen that above with poultices and apply it, and do not remove it while it is like this, for the medicine has not yet been absorbed by it until it is healed.
And sometimes make this alone, when you are not present with dragon's blood and dragon's wound.
And then do this same operation on large wounds when it is necessary to pause over those and compress them, and on fresh wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in the time of summer, then you should not think about the position of this powder, but rather cure those with what we have said, by applying poultices that are suitable for them, or by applying fine powder made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until a poultice forms; and accordingly cure those with another remedy until they are healed.
But if it occurs in a fracture of the bone, and is small, then you should extract that with gauze.
And I say the cure for fractures of the head in this way which follows.
Of the plagues of the neck.
But if the plague occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in medication and between the plague of the head when it is simple.
But if the nerves of the neck are cut or an artery is injured, then if it is a nerve, do not intervene with poultice, but rather avoid curing it with anything that causes vehement stiptication, just like vinegar and egg whites, which are like vitriol and similar to theirs, which hurt the nerves and contract that. And do not apply anything to the wound that is too cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is in the brain, which is the highest part of all the members.
And if the wound is cured with gentle medicines, just as it is washed with lukewarm water, some times infused in rose oil or not-rose oil, and thus when it is washed with lukewarm water and other parts are softened according to this manner, and poultices moist.
But if the wound is large, then administer a suture, or tie off the edges of it, and accordingly cure that with poultices until it is healed.
But if the wound is deep or occurs in the lowest part of the poultice, then pierce that in the most suitable location.
But if an artery has been cut in the wound and blood is flowing, then separate or dry it out, or tie it off, or cauterize it if necessity demands that too.
But if the vertebrae of the neck have been cut or all, and the veins of the neck are saved, then you should adjust the edges of the wound with sutures over the canal of the neck and do not touch that; above equalize that and reduce it to its natural shape, and accordingly strengthen that with decent stricture, and leave it for a few days; and accordingly cure that with poultices in which there is stiptication and excitation until it is healed.
But if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then pierce it, and then if there are fragments of bone, extract all that you can from them; and what is not removable, leave that until the wound settles, and be separate and the excrescence from it be alleviated.
And if the wound is fresh, then powderize over it with the powder that I recommended. But if there is a fistula in the wound, then cure that with what will be remembered later in its own chapter.
If it is a blow from a lance or a cote and sometimes the depth of the wound, then consider more if there is ventilation in the wound when the patient breathes; know that the wound is mortal.
And if there is no depth to the wound and it is recent with its own blood, then you should apply powder to it at the first hour, and not strengthen that so that the blood is not retained in the depth of it and returns to the heart and aches the patient, but rather pause on it an attractive poultice, and remove it twice a day.
And if the poultice is not present, then you should pause on the orifice of the wound with a cloth so that it sucks out what there is of the humidities; and make the patient sleep over the wound so that the water that is in it is adjusted.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound and there is no spasm nor trembling of the heart nor constriction of the artery, and sometimes other good dispositions from it, then know that the wound is saved; and accordingly cure that with cauterization and another remedy until it is healed.
But if the healing of it is delayed, and all time has opened up, then know that a fistula has been formed; cure then that according to its own chapter.
And if the wound is due to incision of space or cote, and is simple on the surface of the foot or hand, then cure that with what has preceded it by suture, if it is great, or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has made an impression in the bone, and there are fragments of bone, then pierce the wound and extract those fragments, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then leave them until the wound settles, so that the extraction of them is alleviated.

Of the wounds of the belly.
The indisposition which occurs in the belly is either great, or small, or middling.
And a small disruption is made difficult by another manner, and you must know that the reduction of them is more difficult, if you do not take care to put their intrusion back into its place soon, for it opens up and becomes engorged so that the instrument of it is made difficult.
And therefore the best disruption is middling, because in that one there is no difficulty in reducing the bowels, just as it is difficult in the two species mentioned before.
And know that the suture of the belly is according to four manners, but two sutures are common that are necessary in sutures of other wounds of the body.
And two other sutures proper communicate with the other wounds, but nevertheless are more proper in the suture of the belly.
And I recommend to you any exposition and declaration.
Therefore I say that when the wound is small and some cause of the bowels has been made by it, and it is difficult to reduce it, then this is done in one of two manners: or by the smallness of the disruption as we have said, or when the bowels have become inflamed due to the coldness of the air.
And therefore when this is so, it is necessary that you scrape that in such a way that you submerge a sponge or damp cloth in hot water alone, or that you soak it in water with squinant, and cypress, and spic, and wrap the bowels around that until the inflammation is resolved.
And sometimes I find that this has a stiptic quality, and it is better than hot water alone in resolving the inflammation.
And therefore when you find that the inflammation is resolved, then you should moisten the bowels with water in which there are high and bitter roots, for by this the instrument of it with little cause.

Of the instrument, see the shape of it:
The one part of it is twisted sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the extremity subtle, and not so subtle as a spatula, but rather obtuse a little.

And this is the common method of suturing: take a needle, or count the needles according to the quantity of the amplitude of the wound; and then leave from the extremity of the disruption of the ring finger, and strengthen the needle one, so that you do not put faith in the two ends of the cord, with the two ends of the ciphac that is left outside the cord, until it penetrates from that part; and you have already added two ends of the cord and two ends of the ciphac, and thus four orders are made.
And accordingly strengthen with double faith in the circuit of the needle, and sometimes from two parts together, and accordingly add the two edges and the wound by decent addition; and accordingly leave the thickness of the finger and put another needle in that place, and accordingly tie that with a thread as if it were a first needle; and do not cease to do this if it is necessary with the needles until you have completed all the constriction of the wound.
And the needles should be middling between coarseness and subtlety, because the fine needles barely cut into the flesh; and the coarse ones are of difficult instrument in the cord, and therefore it is necessary that they be middling in subtlety and coarseness.
And it is not necessary that the needle be inserted in both ends of the cord at once, for fear that the flesh will be cut too little and the wound will become inflamed before its consolidation.
And do not prolong the suturing so that the wound is prohibited from consolidation.
And accordingly insert the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient's rest in his bed; and pause on the suturing with poultices spread out from all sides, which have the ends of the needles; and leave those until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And these species of suture with needles in this manner are more suitable for small wounds, because they suffice in the suture of them with one needle or two or around those.
But the second suture is common: it is that you administer with suturing the four extremities, of the cord and two extremities of the ciphac, in one go, with a needle in which the thread is wrapped evenly in subtlety and coarseness.
And accordingly, when you have the needle penetrate these four extremities, reduce the needle to that middle part from which it began, in order that the thread may be pulled back from the most elevated part of the wound to the wound itself, in order that the suture may be according to the suture of cloth with which the cloths are strengthened.
And pause between each suture the quantity of the thickness of the little finger.
And this suture is known to men.

On the cure of abscesses and fistulas.
Know that every wound and apostema when it becomes old and antiquated, and is made an ulcer, and is not consolidated and grows a hard crust all the time and is not cut off, then, regardless of what member it may be in, universally it is called fistula and we call it abscess.
And fistula according to truth is a nodular abscess, hard, white, and painless, with which there is no pain and it is as if the cavity of the abscess were the penalty of the owl; and for this reason they called that "rizatz", i.e. penalty.
And it is in some men moist, which grows a crust; and the moisture is soon absorbed in a few hours. And sometimes this moisture is more abundant, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
And now I have shown all those causes, and their signs, and the cure of them with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary that you know how to treat fistulas which are made by way of operation with me.
And know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body, because some are fistulas that penetrate into the great veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the ciphac, or the bowel, or the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to some of the vertebrae of the back, or to any of the joints composed by composition as is the case with the hand and foot; and those are which give proximity to the main member and its likenesses.
And therefore, that one of these fistulas which is according to this manner is one of the difficult-to-heal diseases, and does not receive healing, and its occupation with it is toil and ignorance.
And if some of the fistulas have a depth that does not reach those places I mentioned, and you wait and hope for its healing, and wish to understand it, then take a try with iron or steel, and if the fistula follows the natural path, then explore it with the finger.
But if the fistula is twisted, then investigate it with a subtle lead, because lead with the lightness of its own body is alleviated and curved in such a way that it follows the twisting.
And if the fistula has many horrible appearances, it is not possible for you to signify on it with a probe.
Then clean the orifice by its own orifices, because the moisture which you use to cleanse it flows through the other orifices and drains from them.
And accordingly, inquire exquisitely, according to the manner in which it is possible for you to know if there are bones or nerves here, and whether the fistula is distant or near, or if it is one of those many orifices that is situated above this entire sum of your strength, with your introspection, with which you reflect on the patient, and the invention of pain due to your compression with your hand on the location, and similar signs and causes of accidents affecting the apostema.
And when you have stood on all those causes with steadfast true understanding, then go to the cure according to confidence: and it is that you consider now whether it is an apparent fistula near or in a salubrious location, distant from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places which I teach you and say.

And I recommend to you that you attempt to heal a man whose toe is affected by this accident which we and you have recounted, which is when it becomes black in his foot with an inflammation that was assembled as if by the combustion of fire.
And that corruption began first in his toe and spread throughout the foot.
And then that man prepared himself for the possibility that pus would come out and the cure would go to the member with the vehemence of his pain and inflammation of it, and he cut off that foot at the junction, and it became healthy.
For a long time, that corruption had spread to the finger of his hand.
And then it came to me, and thus I perceived the surplus of that corruption above which was suspended over his hand with regard to the medicines, so that the purging of his body began; and no longer was the surplus reflected back, but instead it began to move towards another finger in his hand.
And he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do that, hoping instead for the reflection of that surplus back onto itself, but rather fearing the amputation of his hand, since the patient's vital force was already at a low ebb.
And since he departed from me, he returned to his land and reported to me that the man had prepared and cut off his entire hand, and it was healed.
And I have not narrated this story except to serve as an aid for those who seek to understand this disease, and to provide a signification by which it may be interpreted and acted upon.
The care of wounds and the quality of cleansing with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some flesh and the space of the abscess is prolonged to form a collection of pus, and it is broken and perforated, and the pus is discharged from it, and the location remains open like a vessel, with a covering that is like thin cloth, and there is no further corruption, and it does not penetrate into bone or nerve or ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not named fistula.
But if the space is prolonged to the point where corruption enters into some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the cure for this is that you cut out that covering entirely, as it is revolved, and especially when it is thinned out and made like cloth, and make sure that it does not stick to the location due to its corruption.
But if you think that the covering will stick and that the corruption has not had its due consequence, and in the covering there has been a change of direction, then you cure that with poultice.
And so you consider the sinus, and then if it is large, and the arm that you have is of the kind that gives off an odor, then apply poultice to that with Egyptian medicine which is made from oil, vinegar, and zingiber receiving equal parts, and be adjusted in a vessel, and be poured over the fire until the medicine becomes rough and turns into a substance like honey.
And then you take from it the water that is necessary and dissolve it with equal parts of water and honey; and apply poultice to that sinus, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine in it for the amount of two hours.
And then you extract that abscess; and make it so for as many days as is necessary until the sinus is cleansed and the stench is removed.
And sometimes it is applied with ash water, when this medicine is not present; and it is that you take the ash of vines, and put it on top of water; and then mix it together and apply poultice to that with it until you are convinced that the sinus is closed.
And if the patient does not have tolerance for Egyptian medicine or ash water, then apply poultice to that with honey and water mixed with a small amount of zingiber shredded, and then apply poultice to that with vinegar and honey mixed, because the property of honey is that it purifies and cleanses, and vinegar makes the sinus adhere, and especially when in vinegar there is an excess of stiptic and drying properties.
And when you do this several times and are convinced that the sinus is now removed, then apply poultice to that with water that makes the skin appear in it.
And it is that you take from the divine dyafinicon and dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic vinegar; or that you apply poultice to that with several medicines and other substances that have properties such as those which I have already written in the treatise on medicines.
And if the opening of the sinus is narrow and cannot receive the canula of the poultice, then you amplify that with a small iron tool bit by bit, and pause in it wrapped in Egyptian or basilic cloth until it is amplified.
And similarly, if the opening is wide, then you add the lips of it with a suture and leave it in such quantity that the poultice can be added to it.
And if the opening of that from which the arm flows is elevated to the parts above, then dry that in the lowest part of it so that the arm flows into it, because when the arm is constricted in the swelling of the sinus, the flesh will be generated in it.
And if it is not possible to dry the sinus within the environs of the bone, then you should perforate the member with preparation for which the arm will flow slightly according to your apparel and that there be no reason in it for the arm to be retained.
But that which is on the opening of the sinus, which remains in all its hour because it is adjusted to the arm. And so that you can know if what comes out from the arm is much or little, or is digested, or is not digested.
And at this point you consider the location of that sinus, if in it the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess.
And when your medication is prolonged in this way, and you see the matter that is dropped on the opening of the sinus already sticking or approaching adhesion, then dry it out with a cloth or a small tool on the third day, and when you remove the dressing, then change the cloth for another and renew the poultice.
But if from the sinus there is too little space for a subtle virus to be present, then do not despair of its adhesion, because the healing of it is approaching, because some people in whom tardy generation of flesh occurs in their wounds, and others are in those in which the opposite occurs.
And if from the sinus it takes many days for an undigested arm to be present, then you will know that the sinus does not adhere; and if the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and is the cause prolonged, then you adjust in exsiccation of medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and virtue, they are dried out like enguent dyafinicon, when there is an excessive addition of zegi.
And the most later of all is that which is cured, that you take from dyafinicon and dissolve it in rose oil, and apply it to the wound with an old equal substance, and then confirm that on it, and use that.
And it seems so in that action, when there is no brac, dyafinicon, and honey when it is mixed into being thickened, and use it; or that you take myrrh and aloen and onions, and grind everything together and powderize it over the honey when it is on the fire, and then line it up with water on cloth and stretch it over the sinus; and line it up with the honey which has been mixed into being thickened, and powderize it on cloth and stretch it.
And some times it is administered at the aristological long and razed of celestial lily (and it is celestial lily) and farina of errors and centaurea, and use those simples or adjust them, grind them together and powderize them over the honey which has been recounted; and husk it.
And if the sinus is prolonged and does not heal with this treatment, then you will know that the corruption is in the preon of it, and already inquiry is made in the bones or in the other hard members or ligaments; then you cure it with fistular treatment, just as above is said.
Of the cure of panarici, and unguis attritae, and incision of finger added, and section.
Panarici is an abscess that leaves behind the nail of the toe or finger, and spreads quickly to other fingers, and when it is prolonged and its cure is less valued, or it becomes apostematized with caution, or it becomes corrupted, and throws forth brackish water within which corrodes the root of the nail, and quickly corrupts that entirely, and quickly pervades its corruption to the bone, and makes a fetid odor, and causes the extremity of the finger to become gangrenous.
And therefore when you have that which we have said in the division and do not confirm your cure, then it is necessary that you inscribe with iron all the superfluitat that remains of the nail and appropriate cauterize the wound with water, for cauterization is most helpful in this case.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and the adductions of the nail are already compressing the flesh to the parts outside, and begin to prick and lead it away from that place, then you must pause a fine ray below the angle of the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it up and inscribe it into the flesh with ease, and pause over what remains of the flesh of the medicines combining corrosive substances until it is all removed; and then cure that with poultices until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already taken hold in the bone, then you must inscribe the bone and extract it, for no time is there healing that is corrupted in the bone.
And if at times the corrosion and corruption go into the digit, then you must inscribe it in one of the joints according to the premonition of its reminiscence, and appropriate cure that until it is healed.
But if the nail is inflamed with percussion or attrition, and inflames in that place with a vehement pain, then you must first fleubotomize the malady, and then secate the nail with a sharp spatula in a transverse section from top to bottom, and be careful not to allow the section to penetrate into the flesh that is left behind the nail, for you would make the malady cause a vehement pain, and thus cause unnecessary birth of superfluous flesh in that place; and then cure that place with what relieves pain.
But it is said that this adjustment is natural in many men, and for many is all flesh, or for many is in the bones, or for many is in the nail.
And some of them are born in the root of the joint, or is the birthplace of them in certain joints of the fingers. But that which is born in certain joints of the finger does not become mad, and that which is born in the junctures is very much maddened.
And from those who are born of flesh, the section is easy, and it is that you must inscribe the root with a sharp spatula.
But from those who are born in the root of the joint, the cure is difficult; and therefore beware of the abscess of it.
But in that which is born of the digit, thou must first cut off the joints, and then inscribe with a round instrument into the bone, and afterwards saw with one of those saws suitable for this, and then cure that until it is healed.
But the consolidation that occurs in the fingers between their joints or due to the nativity of the human being who is born with it, or due to the consolidation of a wound or due to combustion by fire, or for similar reasons, therefore you must cut away that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural form.
And then pause between their folds with a little oil rose for not being consolidated lightly, and separate those, or pause between those one thin layer of lead so that it is consolidated according to what is needed.
And similarly if consolidation occurs in some fingers at the palm, then you must cut away that consolidation according to what is prepared and conforms to the shape of the member.
Of the inscription of vice, there are several.
Vices are varicas, and so are veins enveloped in thick, full of superfluous melancholic fluids that come forth from the members of the body, and the most common occurrence of theirs is in the hips, and especially in the hips of travelers, laborers, and carriers.
Therefore it is necessary that you administer purgation of the body with black cholera several times with strong expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the Basilic vein.
But the cure of theirs with iron is according to two methods: one is that you inscribe and attract that black blood, and the other method is that you elevate the vein and extract all.
The section of this is according to this method: first, take the hip with cold water and make it moist until the thick blood is resolved, which is turbid from the hip, and then strengthen the hip of the patient at the highest point of the coccyx, and above that, above the denounment, with a bandage, and then cut off the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide section, and then raise the black blood by the tieua of the partition below the hip, from top to bottom, until the desired quantity of blood is removed, which takes away the virtue of the patient.
And then lie down, and command to him that he abstain from foods that generate black cholera.
And iterate the cure by phlebotomy when the veins are filled and this is noticed to the patient.
But the elevation of theirs is according to this method: you who raise the hip of the patient, if it is covered with moss (mots pels), and then put it in a bath and wrap the hip with cold water until it becomes red and the veins are filled; or that he be exercised by strong exercise, even without bath, until the member is warm.
And then cut the cord (codena) in the right side of the vein for a section in the long or end part of it, or in the lower part of it, you should make the hole (lo talo).
And then fill the cord (codena) with unguents and scrape off the vein from all parts until it appears to the sensation, and be aware of that which times that part often asks for darkness.
And thus, as you take away (cum evazeys) the cord (codena), and the white substance that is cord-like (quays sia corda).
And then you must put away that which is the way (le ray) so that it may be elevated and thrown away from the cord (codena), and suspend it with a hook (orp) like a lion.
And then you must make another section (seccio) near that section for three fingers (ditz), and then scrape off the cord (codena) from the upper part of the vein until it appears.
And then you must elevate that and inscribe it in the rear section of the talo (le talo), and then extract it and elevate it until it is emerged through the second section, and then extract it from the section above.
And then do this until you extract it from the highest or uppermost section of all the sections, until everything is emerged; and then inscribe it.
And if it does not obey your order to extract and elevate, then insert a needle with a strong double thread and bind it (ligua aquela) and extract it, or insert below it the way and revolve your hand around the entire area until it is gone. And be careful that it is not torn (inscidida); for if it is broken, it will become difficult for you to elevate that part and it will come back upon the patient as a nuisance.
And when all that has been removed (tota) is fully gone, then pause over the place of the wound, submerged in wine and rose oil and non-rose oil, and cure it until it is healed.
And if the vein is contracted and twisted (tortuositat) without a normal curvature, and it is not straight according to what we have said, then you must cut across that part of tortuosity of yours and at the places where there is curvature, and then suspend it with unguents until you elevate it all.
And beware that your incision (seccio) does not cut into the vein and does not injure it, for then it would be difficult for you to elevate it; and exercise caution in that.
The shape of the incision that is made with the blood:
It is not like that of a hook or scissors, nor has it an acute extremity so as to injure the vein; but rather it has a thick and flexible lion-like shape, because if it were too subtle, it would cut into the vein due to its subtlety; and it has in excess a thickness similar to what we have said.
The extraction of the saphenous vein.
This vein is generated in the hips (cambas) in cold lands, as Al-Ategi said in the land of Arabs and in dry lands with little moisture and in those where there is no grass nor river.
And it is also generated in other parts of the body beyond the hips.
And its generation is from putrefaction that remains after the cord (codena) as well as venom poured out from the body of serpents, worms, and scorpions, and worms generated between the cord and the flesh.
And the sign of the susceptibility to the coming of it is when this vein in the hip becomes inflamed with great fervor; and at that place, vesicles form; and then the vein begins to emerge from that location where it appears as if a plant has taken root.
And then, when the extremity appears from him, you must wrap around it a leaden cloth of which one ounce weighs two drams, and anoint it and let the lead hang from the hip.
And whenever you find some cause at the outer parts (partidas), wrap it in lead and bind it. And if the part is prolonged (mot es prolonguat), you must incise one part of it and wrap up the remainder; and do not cut into that which has a root (de razit) until it is fully gone, for if you cut into it, it will be contracted and enter into the flesh and cause apostema and burning in that place and bad ulceration.
Therefore, it is necessary to treat it gently and extract it little by little, until it is fully removed from the body and there is no remaining cause in the body.
And from this vein, some men have been extracted who are in its length of 20 palms and I have already seen one who was 30 palms.
And if it is incised at the time of its medication (hora de la sua medicacio), then you must introduce the ray into the track of it and pierce that part with a long track through the body, until all that which is in the material is evacuated, and administer putrefaction of the place for some days with medicines; and then cure that part by the cure of apostemas.
And this vein sometimes has many branches (motz ramps), and especially when it appears at the junction of the foot or in the foot, and comes out with many orifices (orrificis), and is issued from each orifice a branch.
And therefore, cure that part just like we have said in the division and also as has been said above.
On the removal of worms generated under the skin and it is called Bovine Ailment.
This illness is called in some lands the Bovine Ailment because many times it appears to be related to oxen and there is a worm that is born between the cord (codena) and the flesh, which goes throughout the body rising and falling, and is felt by the sensation of the own affection for limb to limb until it breaks the cord and comes out.
And the generation of this worm is due to putrefaction (putrefaccio) of certain humors, just like it happens with worms and serpents and lizards and scorpions in the womb.
And it is feared for the malice of this worm, because when it enters the body and rises to the head, and reaches the brain, then it is very strong in it and goes into it and destroys it, and that ends many times.
And therefore, when you want to cure that and extract it, then do not proceed if you do not have the patient's consent and appearance of the wound (sentiment), and thus it is necessary to stretch what is above it and what is left of it with gentle constriction, and then bind over it and extract that.
And if it is buried in the flesh and you do not remove it, then you must pause the cauterizing iron with fire on the location until it dies, and the greatest fear that is feared is the corruption of the surrounding area which corrupts the location just as we have said.
And if you find that the worm has reached the head near the brain, then strengthen the scalp with a strong stricture, and then bind over it, and extract it; and it is necessary for the patient to use the purification of their body with medicines evacuating bad humors, and beware of foods that generate putrefaction.
On the removal of worms from the skin (sectione super aegritudinem nafir).
This disease is called "nafir" in our land, and it is pain that comes to some members, and is spread from member to member.
And you already know it, as I have recommended it to you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I discovered her arm and saw a small swelling in the vein at the end of the arm, and after being there for an hour, I saw that swelling go away just like worms rise up to this place, but more slowly than it should be, as if it were live silver when it flows from place to place.
And then I went back to the pain in that place and fixed myself into the muscle, and there stayed for an hour.
And then I corrected it in another direction until I reached the other arm.
And then I told myself that it was revolving itself around the entire body according to what you saw; and it was too marvelous the transformation of it and the speed from member to member. And I had already seen this before in my own flesh according to that manner; however, I have seen many others which also suffer from being transformed from member to member. But I did not see it in the same way with my own flesh as I saw it in the woman.
And I didn't think it was this way, but rather it is because the woman was old, with few seconds and veins uncovered, and in this appearance, that ventosity became perceptible.
And it is necessary that this condition does not appear according to this retrograde course in those who are delicacies and have humid hearts with veins hardened.
And when you want the cure of that, and the patient feels that pain, then it is not apparent to you what is happening at the top as we have said, but you must strengthen over that and leave it slightly open and dry over that until that ventosity is blocked, and cauterize the place.
But if you do not treat it with the right pulse, then you must cure that with excitement of the chest and with what expels ventosity, and charm those with foul pills and with pills of serape and similar ones.
Of the removal of thorns.
Thorns are diversified according to species, and according to the locations of the body where they grow, because their diversity is that some have great points, small ones, concave ones, dull ones, which are solid; and some have three angles, and those with tongues; and those with stars.
And among the signs of the servant is when it caters in the sageta, and trespasses the bone, and is situated above the cyphac which is on the brain, because accident occurs due to soda vehement, scotomia, vertigo, and roar in the ears, and inflammation and roar of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding and vomiting of gall, and it is very much destroyed the word and is ruined the voice, and there is situated above the wound a humid white substance similar to powder, and there is an appearance of water like the flesh.
And therefore, if these signs appear to you, then it is necessary that you abstain from the cure and extraction of the thorn, unless it is outside.
But the signs of the thorn when it caters in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if something has been placed there in a hard cause, and not a soft one; and very soon the movement of the thorn is like the movement of the pulse, and flows from the wound black blood, and there is a feeling of coldness in the extremities, and a shivering sensation, and fainting; and therefore know that death is descending upon you completely.
And the signs when the thorn has pierced the lung are that blood foam comes from the wound, and the vessels near the neck become inflamed, and the patient's complexion changes, and the spirit breathes heavily, and asks for fresh air.
And if the thorn pierces the membrane which is in the feet, and the pain is then near the small ribs, and it makes a great loud noise with violent pain and sighing, and none of the members of the muscles can be moved.
And if the thorn pierces the stomach, then very soon there will be some undigested food coming out of the wound.
And if the thorn pierces the belly and is stuck there, then some gap or tear in the wound, or the membrane or bladder which is broken, and there is no hope for the cure of the extraction of the thorn.
And if the thorn pierces the bladder and is voided outside as urine, and processes some cause to the parts outside, and very soon there is pain on the patient, then you should know that it is mortal.
But other members such as the face, neck, and groin, and the shoulders and assistants, and the vertebrae of the back, and the furcula, and the coccyx, and the hip and its likenesses to the members, are saved according to the greatest dispositions when the thorn does not touch a vein or artery and is not a venomous thorn.
And I tell you this, that I have seen the being of these thorns, and for what it signifies for the cure of this illness.
The cause is that when the thorn pierces in the lacrimal of the eye socket in the root of the nose, and I extract it from the other side, leaving the gray matter of the ear behind, and he recovers, and does not suffer any harm to the eye.
And I extracted another thorn from a Jew, which had pierced him in the gray matter of his eye socket, leaving behind the eyelid plus further, and the thorn was already hidden and not visible except for a small extremity with which it adhered to his fist, and it was a great thorn of the sharp thorns of the Turks, like a lion's claw without ears.
And the Jew sat, and did not suffer any harm in his eye.
And I extracted another thorn from a Christian man, which was lodged in the groin area, and it was an Arab thorn, and it had ears; and then I incised above that one between two guides, and it was already submerged in his groin; and then I carefully extracted it, and he is now healed, the Christian.
And I extracted another thorn from a man, which was lodged in his stomach, and thought that he would die because of it; and therefore, since more than 30 days had passed and there was no change in his condition, I incised above the thorn and operated on it, and he is now healed, and not affected by the harm.
And I saw a man in whom a thorn had pierced the spine of his back, and the wound was consolidated on him, and after almost seven years, the thorn came out at the root of the backbone.
And I saw a woman in whom a thorn had pierced her stomach, and the wound was consolidated on the inside of her, and it had not changed in her condition for many years, and the woman did not experience any harm or difficulty with any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man in whom a thorn had pierced his face and the wound was consolidated and the thorn remained, not causing any great pain or resembling those.
And I extracted the thorn from the king's nose, which was lodged in the middle of his nose and had already declined to the right side by a small amount, and the whole thorn was hidden.
And I was summoned for the treatment of him within three days after the thorn entered.
And then I examined the wound of the thorn very carefully; and then I inquired about it with subtle attempts, and did not feel any pain; but he felt a pricking sensation behind his right earlobe, and then I suspected that this prick was from the extremity of the thorn.
And I applied the ointment to the place where it is virtuous for attracting and digestion, believing that the place is inflamed because of the thorn's presence, and that it needs to be cleansed over that area.
And there was no significant accident in the place where the thorn had managed to reach that location; and I continued to apply the ointment on him for many days, and there was no accident; and the wound consolidated in the meantime, and the patient's malady from the exit of his nose remained for several days until one day he felt the thorn inside his nose and recognized it again.
And then I applied to the wound acute corrosive medicine for many days until it was fully open, and with the attempt, I carefully extracted that extremity of the thorn which adhered to his fist.
And then I adjusted in the appearance of the wound with that acute medicine until it became visible to me as the extremity of the thorn, and passed on to something else with this space of time within four months.
And then as the wound became amplified, and I had the possibility to enter it with forceps, and remain there, and not obey any orders, but rather, I continued to subtilize and engineer on that spot using the methods of engineering, until one day on that spot using the methods of engineers, taking him with descending forceps, according to the shape of those in the end of the capital, within which I extracted it; and then restored that wound.
And some doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose was not restored, and I restored it and the wound is consolidated, and the patient is healed by whole health, and there is no damage to him in any cause.
And I recommend to you the quality of extraction of some thorns because it is necessary that you pause here and consider the rule and significance of what has been said, for the parts of this art and the definitions of that are not comprehended by narration or free speech.
And the artisans know well how to compare a little with much, and on what is present with what is absent; and they find new operation and new instruments that are necessary for the descent of external causes from art when accidents occur.
And therefore, I say that thorns are not expelled from the members in which they are stuck, except according to two ways: or by attraction of the place where they entered; or by contrary motion of the other part.
And that which is expelled by the place where it entered, or is a thorn proceeding from a fleshly location, and is attracted and expelled.
And if it does not obey the sign of the hour in which it was caught, then you should leave it for some days until the flesh around it becomes putrid, and the attraction to it and its exit are alleviated.
And similarly, if it is stuck in bone and does not obey your sign, then leave it for some days and iterate the attraction and motion every day, and it will be expelled.
And if it does not obey your sign after some days, then you should pierce the circuit of the thorn in that bone on all sides with a subtle tool until the location is amplified by the thorn, and then extract it.

And when you administer the extraction of the thorn in every location where it is, then you should use with twisting of your hand and forceps on all sides until it complies; and subtlety with subtle delicacy that the thorn is not broken and that it is made to fit your difficult attraction to it and its extraction.
And if you cannot do anything about that of your hour, then you should leave for some days until the parts that are in the circle of it become settled, and then iterate again when it is alleviated. But if there is contrary flow of blood to you, then you should administer the water that we have said in our chapter on cure.
And take care of your virtue of inscizio of vein or nerve or cord, and administer skill in every manner possible to the evasion of the thorn; and do this with facility and tranquility and slowness and firmness as you have recommended.
And therefore, that you may counteract the thorn in such a way that the malady is according to the figure according to which you are forced to cauterize the thorn in it, because it is more justifiable. But if this is not possible for you, then you should administer what is possible to you according to the figures.
But the thorns that are expelled by the contrary of the other part, or which already have proceeded some part to the parts outside, or make softness (gillibositat) at the extremity of the thorn due to the sensation of the part above the codena propdana and sometimes elevated; then you should see over it; and be the section according to the quantity in which the forceps take hold; and properly attract it, because it is made light for a sign.
But if it is retained in the bone, then you should twist the thread (lama) according to contrary motion until the thorn (sageta) presses into the bone, and amplify as far as possible, and properly extract that.
And if not, then leave that for some days, and properly iterate that until it is consumed.
And if the root of the thorn is in that place, then you should push it into place.
But if the root is cut and you must administer impulse, then you should introduce it into that place, even if it is deaf, using a hidden instrument so that it enters the concavity of it in the tail of the thorn and properly push it into place.
But if the thorn is concave, then you should push it into place with a strong instrument entering into that, because the thorn is alleviated by that.
But if the thorn is embedded, then you should cover all the flesh where it is located, if that is possible to you, and properly care for it with what is necessary.
And if the thorn (sageta) is stuck in the foot, or in the belly, or in the bladder, or in the ribcage, and it is close enough that you can touch it with your hand, and it is possible to see over it, then look over it and take care not to damage any veins or nerves, and extract it, and properly cover the wound if necessary, and cure it until it is healed.
Forma of forceps by which are attracted thorns:
The extremities (ends) of which are like the beak of an owl, and are made as if they were a saw when they take hold on the thorn so that it does not let go.
And there are many species, great, few, and mid-sized, according to the quantity of greatness of the thorn and its smallness, and the width of the wound, and the constriction of it.
